# Architecture Q&A: Envoy HTTP Filter Chain

**Repository:** envoyproxy/envoy
**Task Type:** Architecture Q&A (investigation only — no code changes)

## Background

Envoy is a high-performance service proxy that processes HTTP requests through a layered filter architecture. Understanding how a request flows from initial TCP accept through to the upstream server is fundamental to working with Envoy's codebase.

## Questions

Answer ALL of the following questions about Envoy's HTTP request processing pipeline:

### Q1: Listener to Connection Manager

When a downstream client opens a TCP connection to Envoy, how does the listener hand off the connection to the HTTP connection manager? Specifically:
- What mechanism selects which network filter chain to use for an incoming connection?
- How is the HTTP connection manager (`ConnectionManagerImpl`) installed as a network filter?
- What happens in `onData()` when the first bytes arrive?

### Q2: HTTP Filter Chain Creation and Iteration

Once HTTP request headers are parsed, how does Envoy build and iterate through the HTTP filter chain?
- At what point in request processing is the HTTP filter chain created?
- In what order are decoder filters invoked vs. encoder filters?
- What return values can a filter use to control iteration (stop, continue, buffer)?

### Q3: Router and Upstream

How does the router filter (the terminal HTTP filter) forward requests to upstream servers?
- How does the router obtain the target cluster and select a specific upstream host?
- What is the role of `UpstreamRequest` and the upstream filter chain?
- How does the response flow back through the filter chain to the downstream client?

### Q4: Architectural Boundaries

Explain the distinction between these two "filter chain" concepts in Envoy:
- The network-level filter chain (managed by `FilterChainManager`)
- The HTTP-level filter chain (managed by `FilterManager`)

Why are they separate, and how do they relate to each other?

## Output Requirements

Write your answer to `/logs/agent/investigation.md` with the following structure:


108-assistanttext-
The investigation is complete. I've written the report to `/logs/agent/investigation.md` covering all four questions with specific file paths, class names, and function references. Here's a summary of the findings:

**Q1 (Listener → Connection Manager):** TCP connections are accepted by `ActiveTcpListener::onAccept()`, go through listener filters via `ActiveTcpSocket`, then `FilterChainManagerImpl::findFilterChain()` selects the network filter chain using a multi-level matching hierarchy (destination port/IP, SNI, ALPN, source type/IP/port). The HCM is installed as a `Network::ReadFilter` via `createNetworkFilterChain()`. On first bytes, `onData()` creates the HTTP codec lazily and dispatches data through it.

**Q2 (HTTP Filter Chain):** The HTTP filter chain is created per-stream inside `ActiveStream::decodeHeaders()` after route resolution, by calling `createDownstreamFilterChain()`. Decoder filters iterate in configuration order (A→B→C), encoder filters iterate in reverse order (C→B→A). Filters control iteration via status codes like `Continue`, `StopIteration`, `StopAllIterationAndBuffer`, and `StopAllIterationAndWatermark`.

**Q3 (Router & Upstream):** The router filter gets the cluster via `ClusterManager::getThreadLocalCluster()`, selects a host via `cluster->chooseHost(this)`, and creates an `UpstreamRequest` with a `GenericConnPool`. The `UpstreamRequest` manages the upstream filter chain via `UpstreamFilterManager`. Responses flow back through `onUpstreamHeaders()` which calls `callbacks_->encodeHeaders()`, entering the encoder filter chain in reverse order.

**Q4 (Architectural Boundaries):** Network filter chains are per-connection, selected at accept time based on connection metadata, and operate on raw bytes. HTTP filter chains are per-stream, created when

  "content": "# Envoy HTTP Filter Chain Architecture\n\n## Q1: Listener to Connection Manager\n\n### How the listener accepts a TCP connection and hands it off\n\nWhen a downstream client opens a TCP connection to Envoy, the OS-level accept is handled by `ActiveTcpListener::onAccept()` (`source/common/listener_manager/active_tcp_listener.cc:80`). This method performs connection limit checks, then calls `onAcceptWorker()` (line 109), which optionally rebalances the connection across worker threads via `ConnectionBalancer::pickTargetHandler()` (line 120-125). If the connection stays on the current worker, it creates an `ActiveTcpSocket` and calls `onSocketAccepted()`.\n\nThe `ActiveTcpSocket` (`source/common/listener_manager/active_tcp_socket.h:28`) acts as a `ListenerFilterManager` and runs listener filters (e.g., TLS inspector, proxy protocol) before the connection proceeds. Once listener filters complete, `ActiveTcpSocket::newConnection()` is called, which delegates to `ActiveStreamListenerBase::newConnection()`.\n\n### Network filter chain selection\n\nThe mechanism that selects which network filter chain to use is `FilterChainManagerImpl::findFilterChain()` (`source/common/listener_manager/filter_chain_manager_impl.h:193`). This is called at `source/common/listener_manager/active_stream_listener_base.cc:30`:\n\n```cpp\nconst auto filter_chain = config_->filterChainManager().findFilterChain(*socket, *stream_info);\n```\n\n`FilterChainManagerImpl` uses a multi-level matching hierarchy to select the appropriate filter chain based on connection properties:\n1. **Destination port** (`DestinationPortsMap`)\n2. **Destination IP** (`DestinationIPsTrie`)\n3. **Server name** (SNI) (`ServerNamesMap`)\n4. **Transport protocol** (`TransportProtocolsMap`)\n5. **Application protocol** (ALPN) (`ApplicationProtocolsMap`)\n6. **Direct source IP** (`DirectSourceIPsTrie`)\n7. **Source type** (local/external) (`SourceTypesArray`)\n8. **Source IP** (`SourceIPsTrie`)\n9. **Source port** (`SourcePortsMap`)\n\nAlternatively, if a `FilterChainMatcher` (xDS matcher) is configured, selection is done via `findFilterChainUsingMatcher()` (`filter_chain_manager_impl.h:224`). If no filter chain matches, the `default_filter_chain_` is used as fallback (`filter_chain_manager_impl.h:218-219`).\n\n### How ConnectionManagerImpl is installed as a network filter\n\nEach matched `FilterChainImpl` (`filter_chain_manager_impl.h:122`) contains a `NetworkFilterFactoriesList` (field `filters_factory_` at line 162). After filter chain selection, `ActiveStreamListenerBase::newConnection()` calls:\n\n```cpp\nconst bool empty_filter_chain = !config_->filterChainFactory().createNetworkFilterChain(\n    *server_conn_ptr, filter_chain->networkFilterFactories());\n```\n(`source/common/listener_manager/active_stream_listener_base.cc:56-57`)\n\nThe `createNetworkFilterChain()` function (`envoy/network/filter.h:988`) iterates through the factory list and creates network filters, adding them to the connection. The HTTP Connection Manager (HCM) is one such network filter \u2014 it is instantiated by its registered factory (configured as `envoy.filters.network.http_connection_manager`) and added to the connection as a `Network::ReadFilter`.\n\n`ConnectionManagerImpl` inherits from `Network::ReadFilter` (`source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.h:61`), so once installed, it receives raw byte data from the connection.\n\n### What happens in onData() when the first bytes arrive\n\nWhen the first bytes arrive on the connection, `ConnectionManagerImpl::onData()` is called (`source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc:505`). Its behavior:\n\n1. **Codec creation** (lines 507-516): If no codec exists yet (`!codec_`), it calls `createCodec(data)` (line 515). The codec is created via `config_->createCodec()` (line 486), which instantiates the appropriate HTTP codec (HTTP/1.1, HTTP/2) based on the data and configuration. The codec type is determined by the ALPN negotiation result or configuration.\n\n2. **Dispatching data** (lines 518-551): The method enters a dispatch loop calling `codec_->dispatch(data)` (line 522). The codec parses HTTP frames from the raw bytes. For HTTP/1.1, the codec calls back into `ConnectionManagerImpl::newStream()` when a new request is detected, and then invokes `ActiveStream::decodeHeaders()` when headers are fully parsed. For HTTP/2, multiple streams can be created during a single dispatch.\n\n3. **Error handling** (lines 524-535): Buffer flood errors, protocol errors, and overload errors are caught and result in connection closure.\n\n4. **Redispatch for HTTP/1** (lines 545-550): For HTTP/1.x, if the connection is still open with remaining data and no active streams, the dispatch loop repeats to handle pipelined requests.\n\nFor HTTP/3 (QUIC), codec creation happens in `onNewConnection()` (line 560-571) rather than `onData()`, since QUIC handles its own de-multiplexing.\n\n---\n\n## Q2: HTTP Filter Chain Creation and Iteration\n\n### When the HTTP filter chain is created\n\nThe HTTP filter chain is created **during request header processing**, specifically inside `ActiveStream::decodeHeaders()` at `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc:1530-1531`:\n\n```cpp\nconst FilterManager::CreateChainResult create_chain_result =\n    filter_manager_.createDownstreamFilterChain();\n```\n\nThis happens after:\n- Headers are validated (line 1355)\n- Route configuration is snapped (lines 1361-1372)\n- Route is cached (line 1520)\n- Request headers are mutated (line 1500)\n\nBut before the headers are dispatched to the filters (line 1567).\n\n`DownstreamFilterManager::createDownstreamFilterChain()` (`source/common/http/filter_manager.cc:1125`) delegates to `FilterManager::createFilterChain()` (line 1696). This method:\n\n1. Checks for upgrade filter chains first (line 1723)\n2. Falls through to `filter_chain_factory.createFilterChain(callbacks)` (line 1734)\n3. The `FilterChainFactoryCallbacksImpl` inner class (line 981-1035) receives callbacks to add decoder, encoder, and stream filters\n\nFilters are added via:\n- `addStreamDecoderFilter()` \u2014 adds to `decoder_filters_.entries_` (line 989)\n- `addStreamEncoderFilter()` \u2014 adds to `encoder_filters_.entries_` (line 996)\n- `addStreamFilter()` \u2014 adds to both decoder and encoder lists (lines 1003-1006)\n\n### Decoder vs encoder filter invocation order\n\nThe key architectural insight is in `source/common/http/filter_manager.h`:\n\n**Decoder filters** (lines 73-81): Iterate in **configuration order** (A \u2192 B \u2192 C). The `StreamDecoderFilters` struct uses a forward iterator (`std::vector::iterator`).\n\n**Encoder filters** (lines 92-100): Iterate in **reverse configuration order** (C \u2192 B \u2192 A). The `StreamEncoderFilters` struct uses a `reverse_iterator` (`std::vector::reverse_iterator`).\n\nSo for a configuration of `[A, B, C]`:\n- Request path (decode): A \u2192 B \u2192 C (forward)\n- Response path (encode): C \u2192 B \u2192 A (reverse)\n\nAfter chain creation, headers are dispatched to decoder filters via `filter_manager_.decodeHeaders(*request_headers_, end_stream)` (`conn_manager_impl.cc:1567`). The `FilterManager::decodeHeaders()` method (filter_manager.h:738) iterates through decoder filters calling each filter's `decodeHeaders()`.\n\n### Return values controlling iteration\n\nDefined in `envoy/http/filter.h`:\n\n**`FilterHeadersStatus`** (line 38):\n- `Continue` \u2014 continue to the next filter\n- `StopIteration` \u2014 stop iterating; must call `continueDecoding()`/`continueEncoding()` to resume\n- `ContinueAndDontEndStream` \u2014 continue iteration but delay end_stream, allowing the filter to inject a body later\n- `StopAllIterationAndBuffer` \u2014 stop all iteration (headers, data, trailers); buffer incoming data; 413 on overflow\n- `StopAllIterationAndWatermark` \u2014 stop all iteration; use watermarks for flow control\n\n**`FilterDataStatus`** (line 129):\n- `Continue` \u2014 continue; buffered data is flushed\n- `StopIterationAndBuffer` \u2014 stop; buffer data\n- `StopIterationAndWatermark` \u2014 stop; use watermarks for backpressure\n- `StopIterationNoBuffer` \u2014 stop; discard buffered data\n\n**`FilterTrailersStatus`** (line 171):\n- `Continue` \u2014 continue\n- `StopIteration` \u2014 stop; must call `continueDecoding()`/`continueEncoding()` to resume\n\nThe filter's `IterationState` enum (`filter_manager.h:211-218`) tracks the current state: `Continue`, `StopSingleIteration`, `StopAllBuffer`, or `StopAllWatermark`.\n\n---\n\n## Q3: Router and Upstream\n\n### How the router obtains the target cluster and selects a host\n\nThe router filter (`source/common/router/router.h:298`, class `Filter`) is the terminal HTTP decoder filter. Its `decodeHeaders()` method (`source/common/router/router.cc:440`) performs:\n\n1. **Route lookup** (line 471): `route_ = callbacks_->route()` \u2014 obtains the route from the cached route in the `ActiveStream`.\n\n2. **Cluster lookup** (lines 523-534): Gets the thread-local cluster from the cluster manager:\n   ```cpp\n   Upstream::ThreadLocalCluster* cluster =\n       config_->cm_.getThreadLocalCluster(route_entry_->clusterName());\n   ```\n   Returns 503 if the cluster is unknown.\n\n3. **Host selection** (line 700): Calls `cluster->chooseHost(this)` where `this` is the `LoadBalancerContext`. The router implements `Upstream::LoadBalancerContextBase` (line 300), providing methods like `computeHashKey()`, `metadataMatchCriteria()`, `determinePriorityLoad()`, and `hostSelectionRetryCount()` that inform the load balancer's decision.\n\n4. **Connection pool acquisition** (line 756 in `continueDecodeHeaders()`): `createConnPool(*cluster, selected_host)` creates a `GenericConnPool` to obtain an upstream connection.\n\n### The role of UpstreamRequest and the upstream filter chain\n\n`UpstreamRequest` (`source/common/router/upstream_request.h:67`) is created at `router.cc:842`:\n```cpp\nUpstreamRequestPtr upstream_request = std::make_unique<UpstreamRequest>(\n    *this, std::move(generic_conn_pool), can_send_early_data, can_use_http3,\n    allow_multiplexed_upstream_half_close_);\n```\n\nAs documented in the header file comments (lines 42-66), `UpstreamRequest` manages the full lifecycle of forwarding a request to an upstream host:\n\n**Request path**: Data arrives via `acceptHeadersFromRouter()` (line 81), `acceptDataFromRouter()` (line 82), `acceptTrailersFromRouter()` (line 83), and `acceptMetadataFromRouter()` (line 84). These pass data to the `UpstreamFilterManager`, which iterates through upstream HTTP filters until reaching the terminal `UpstreamCodecFilter`. The `UpstreamCodecFilter` sends data to the upstream connection; if the connection isn't ready yet, it returns `StopAllIteration` and the `FilterManager` buffers data.\n\n**Connection establishment**: `UpstreamRequest` implements `GenericConnectionPoolCallbacks`. When the connection pool has a connection ready, `onPoolReady()` (line 120) is called, providing a `GenericUpstream` which wraps the upstream codec stream. When the pool fails, `onPoolFailure()` (line 117) triggers error handling.\n\n**Response path**: Upstream responses arrive via the `UpstreamCodecFilter`'s codec bridge, traverse the upstream filter chain in reverse, and reach `UpstreamRequestFilterManagerCallbacks`'s encode functions. These call through `UpstreamRequest`'s `decodeHeaders()`/`decodeData()`/`decodeTrailers()` methods (lines 96-98), which in turn call the router's `RouterFilterInterface::onUpstream[X]()` methods.\n\n### How the response flows back to the downstream\n\nThe router filter's `onUpstreamHeaders()` (`source/common/router/router.cc:1702`) processes the upstream response:\n\n1. Performs outlier detection (line 1743)\n2. Evaluates retry policy (lines 1760-1801) \u2014 may reset the stream and retry\n3. Checks for internal redirects (lines 1803-1810)\n4. Sets response metadata, finalizes headers (lines 1857-1872)\n5. **Sends the response downstream** via `callbacks_->encodeHeaders(std::move(headers), end_stream, ...)` (line 1878)\n\nThis `encodeHeaders()` call enters the `FilterManager`'s encoder filter chain, which iterates through encoder filters in **reverse configuration order** (C \u2192 B \u2192 A). Similarly, `onUpstreamData()` calls `callbacks_->encodeData()` (line 1903) and `onUpstreamTrailers()` calls `callbacks_->encodeTrailers()`.\n\nAfter all encoder filters have processed the response, the `FilterManagerCallbacks` (implemented by `ActiveStream`) receives the final encoded data. `ActiveStream::encodeHeaders()` (`conn_manager_impl.h:241`) writes the response to the `response_encoder_`, which serializes the HTTP response back to the downstream connection via the codec.\n\n---\n\n## Q4: Architectural Boundaries\n\n### Network-level filter chain (FilterChainManager)\n\nThe network-level filter chain is managed by `FilterChainManagerImpl` (`source/common/listener_manager/filter_chain_manager_impl.h:172`). It operates at the **connection level**:\n\n- **Scope**: One filter chain per TCP connection (selected at connection accept time)\n- **Selection criteria**: Connection metadata \u2014 destination IP/port, source IP/port, SNI, ALPN, transport protocol\n- **Contains**: `FilterChainImpl` (`filter_chain_manager_impl.h:122`) which holds:\n  - A `DownstreamTransportSocketFactory` (for TLS termination)\n  - A `NetworkFilterFactoriesList` (factories for network filters like HCM, TCP proxy, etc.)\n  - Transport socket connect timeout\n- **Selection point**: `findFilterChain()` is called once when the connection is accepted, in `ActiveStreamListenerBase::newConnection()` (line 30 of `active_stream_listener_base.cc`)\n- **Network filters**: Implement `Network::ReadFilter`/`Network::WriteFilter` (`envoy/network/filter.h:42-47`), operating on raw byte streams (`Buffer::Instance`). Return `Network::FilterStatus::Continue` or `StopIteration`.\n\n### HTTP-level filter chain (FilterManager)\n\nThe HTTP-level filter chain is managed by `FilterManager` (`source/common/http/filter_manager.h:679`) and its subclass `DownstreamFilterManager` (line 1172). It operates at the **HTTP stream level**:\n\n- **Scope**: One filter chain per HTTP request/response stream (created per-stream)\n- **Selection criteria**: Route configuration, upgrade type\n- **Contains**: `StreamDecoderFilters` and `StreamEncoderFilters` \u2014 vectors of `ActiveStreamDecoderFilter`/`ActiveStreamEncoderFilter` wrappers\n- **Creation point**: `createDownstreamFilterChain()` is called during `ActiveStream::decodeHeaders()` (conn_manager_impl.cc:1530-1531), after the route is determined\n- **HTTP filters**: Implement `Http::StreamDecoderFilter`/`Http::StreamEncoderFilter`/`Http::StreamFilter` (`envoy/http/filter.h`), operating on structured HTTP data (headers, body chunks, trailers, metadata). Return rich status codes (`FilterHeadersStatus`, `FilterDataStatus`, etc.)\n\n### Why they are separate\n\nThe separation exists because of a fundamental difference in abstraction level and multiplexing:\n\n1. **Multiplexing**: A single TCP connection (one network filter chain) can carry multiple HTTP streams (each with its own HTTP filter chain). HTTP/2 and HTTP/3 multiplex many requests over one connection. The network filter chain handles the connection, while HTTP filter chains handle individual requests.\n\n2. **Protocol independence**: Network filters operate on raw bytes and are protocol-agnostic. They handle concerns like TLS termination, rate limiting at the connection level, and protocol detection. HTTP filters operate on parsed HTTP semantics (headers, bodies, trailers) and handle concerns like routing, authentication, and rate limiting at the request level.\n\n3. **Lifecycle difference**: The network filter chain lives for the duration of the TCP connection. HTTP filter chains are created and destroyed per-request. On a long-lived HTTP/2 connection, hundreds of HTTP filter chains may be created and destroyed while the single network filter chain persists.\n\n### How they relate\n\nThe HTTP Connection Manager (`ConnectionManagerImpl`) is the bridge between the two layers. It is installed as a **network read filter** (inheriting `Network::ReadFilter`), making it part of the network filter chain. Its `onData()` method receives raw bytes from the network layer, feeds them to the HTTP codec, and when the codec signals a new stream (via `newStream()`), creates an `ActiveStream` with a `DownstreamFilterManager` that manages the HTTP-level filter chain for that stream.\n\nThe relationship is hierarchical:\n```\nListener\n  \u2514\u2500\u2500 Network Filter Chain (per connection, selected by FilterChainManager)\n        \u2514\u2500\u2500 Network Filters (e.g., TLS inspector, rate limiter, HCM)\n              \u2514\u2500\u2500 ConnectionManagerImpl (the HCM, a network filter)\n                    \u2514\u2500\u2500 HTTP Codec (H1/H2/H3)\n                          \u2514\u2500\u2500 ActiveStream (per HTTP request)\n                                \u2514\u2500\u2500 HTTP Filter Chain (per stream, managed by FilterManager)\n                                      \u2514\u2500\u2500 HTTP Filters (e.g., auth, rate limit, router)\n                                            \u2514\u2500\u2500 Router Filter (terminal, creates UpstreamRequest)\n```\n\n---\n\n## Evidence\n\n### Key files and classes\n\n| Component | File | Class/Function   "content": "# Envoy HTTP Filter Chain Architecture\n\n## Q1: Listener to Connection Manager\n\n### How the listener accepts a TCP connection and hands it off\n\nWhen a downstream client opens a TCP connection to Envoy, the OS-level accept is handled by `ActiveTcpListener::onAccept()` (`source/common/listener_manager/active_tcp_listener.cc:80`). This method performs connection limit checks, then calls `onAcceptWorker()` (line 109), which optionally rebalances the connection across worker threads via `ConnectionBalancer::pickTargetHandler()` (line 120-125). If the connection stays on the current worker, it creates an `ActiveTcpSocket` and calls `onSocketAccepted()`.\n\nThe `ActiveTcpSocket` (`source/common/listener_manager/active_tcp_socket.h:28`) acts as a `ListenerFilterManager` and runs listener filters (e.g., TLS inspector, proxy protocol) before the connection proceeds. Once listener filters complete, `ActiveTcpSocket::newConnection()` is called, which delegates to `ActiveStreamListenerBase::newConnection()`.\n\n### Network filter chain selection\n\nThe mechanism that selects which network filter chain to use is `FilterChainManagerImpl::findFilterChain()` (`source/common/listener_manager/filter_chain_manager_impl.h:193`). This is called at `source/common/listener_manager/active_stream_listener_base.cc:30`:\n\n```cpp\nconst auto filter_chain = config_->filterChainManager().findFilterChain(*socket, *stream_info);\n```\n\n`FilterChainManagerImpl` uses a multi-level matching hierarchy to select the appropriate filter chain based on connection properties:\n1. **Destination port** (`DestinationPortsMap`)\n2. **Destination IP** (`DestinationIPsTrie`)\n3. **Server name** (SNI) (`ServerNamesMap`)\n4. **Transport protocol** (`TransportProtocolsMap`)\n5. **Application protocol** (ALPN) (`ApplicationProtocolsMap`)\n6. **Direct source IP** (`DirectSourceIPsTrie`)\n7. **Source type** (local/external) (`SourceTypesArray`)\n8. **Source IP** (`SourceIPsTrie`)\n9. **Source port** (`SourcePortsMap`)\n\nAlternatively, if a `FilterChainMatcher` (xDS matcher) is configured, selection is done via `findFilterChainUsingMatcher()` (`filter_chain_manager_impl.h:224`). If no filter chain matches, the `default_filter_chain_` is used as fallback (`filter_chain_manager_impl.h:218-219`).\n\n### How ConnectionManagerImpl is installed as a network filter\n\nEach matched `FilterChainImpl` (`filter_chain_manager_impl.h:122`) contains a `NetworkFilterFactoriesList` (field `filters_factory_` at line 162). After filter chain selection, `ActiveStreamListenerBase::newConnection()` calls:\n\n```cpp\nconst bool empty_filter_chain = !config_->filterChainFactory().createNetworkFilterChain(\n    *server_conn_ptr, filter_chain->networkFilterFactories());\n```\n(`source/common/listener_manager/active_stream_listener_base.cc:56-57`)\n\nThe `createNetworkFilterChain()` function (`envoy/network/filter.h:988`) iterates through the factory list and creates network filters, adding them to the connection. The HTTP Connection Manager (HCM) is one such network filter \u2014 it is instantiated by its registered factory (configured as `envoy.filters.network.http_connection_manager`) and added to the connection as a `Network::ReadFilter`.\n\n`ConnectionManagerImpl` inherits from `Network::ReadFilter` (`source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.h:61`), so once installed, it receives raw byte data from the connection.\n\n### What happens in onData() when the first bytes arrive\n\nWhen the first bytes arrive on the connection, `ConnectionManagerImpl::onData()` is called (`source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc:505`). Its behavior:\n\n1. **Codec creation** (lines 507-516): If no codec exists yet (`!codec_`), it calls `createCodec(data)` (line 515). The codec is created via `config_->createCodec()` (line 486), which instantiates the appropriate HTTP codec (HTTP/1.1, HTTP/2) based on the data and configuration. The codec type is determined by the ALPN negotiation result or configuration.\n\n2. **Dispatching data** (lines 518-551): The method enters a dispatch loop calling `codec_->dispatch(data)` (line 522). The codec parses HTTP frames from the raw bytes. For HTTP/1.1, the codec calls back into `ConnectionManagerImpl::newStream()` when a new request is detected, and then invokes `ActiveStream::decodeHeaders()` when headers are fully parsed. For HTTP/2, multiple streams can be created during a single dispatch.\n\n3. **Error handling** (lines 524-535): Buffer flood errors, protocol errors, and overload errors are caught and result in connection closure.\n\n4. **Redispatch for HTTP/1** (lines 545-550): For HTTP/1.x, if the connection is still open with remaining data and no active streams, the dispatch loop repeats to handle pipelined requests.\n\nFor HTTP/3 (QUIC), codec creation happens in `onNewConnection()` (line 560-571) rather than `onData()`, since QUIC handles its own de-multiplexing.\n\n---\n\n## Q2: HTTP Filter Chain Creation and Iteration\n\n### When the HTTP filter chain is created\n\nThe HTTP filter chain is created **during request header processing**, specifically inside `ActiveStream::decodeHeaders()` at `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc:1530-1531`:\n\n```cpp\nconst FilterManager::CreateChainResult create_chain_result =\n    filter_manager_.createDownstreamFilterChain();\n```\n\nThis happens after:\n- Headers are validated (line 1355)\n- Route configuration is snapped (lines 1361-1372)\n- Route is cached (line 1520)\n- Request headers are mutated (line 1500)\n\nBut before the headers are dispatched to the filters (line 1567).\n\n`DownstreamFilterManager::createDownstreamFilterChain()` (`source/common/http/filter_manager.cc:1125`) delegates to `FilterManager::createFilterChain()` (line 1696). This method:\n\n1. Checks for upgrade filter chains first (line 1723)\n2. Falls through to `filter_chain_factory.createFilterChain(callbacks)` (line 1734)\n3. The `FilterChainFactoryCallbacksImpl` inner class (line 981-1035) receives callbacks to add decoder, encoder, and stream filters\n\nFilters are added via:\n- `addStreamDecoderFilter()` \u2014 adds to `decoder_filters_.entries_` (line 989)\n- `addStreamEncoderFilter()` \u2014 adds to `encoder_filters_.entries_` (line 996)\n- `addStreamFilter()` \u2014 adds to both decoder and encoder lists (lines 1003-1006)\n\n### Decoder vs encoder filter invocation order\n\nThe key architectural insight is in `source/common/http/filter_manager.h`:\n\n**Decoder filters** (lines 73-81): Iterate in **configuration order** (A \u2192 B \u2192 C). The `StreamDecoderFilters` struct uses a forward iterator (`std::vector::iterator`).\n\n**Encoder filters** (lines 92-100): Iterate in **reverse configuration order** (C \u2192 B \u2192 A). The `StreamEncoderFilters` struct uses a `reverse_iterator` (`std::vector::reverse_iterator`).\n\nSo for a configuration of `[A, B, C]`:\n- Request path (decode): A \u2192 B \u2192 C (forward)\n- Response path (encode): C \u2192 B \u2192 A (reverse)\n\nAfter chain creation, headers are dispatched to decoder filters via `filter_manager_.decodeHeaders(*request_headers_, end_stream)` (`conn_manager_impl.cc:1567`). The `FilterManager::decodeHeaders()` method (filter_manager.h:738) iterates through decoder filters calling each filter's `decodeHeaders()`.\n\n### Return values controlling iteration\n\nDefined in `envoy/http/filter.h`:\n\n**`FilterHeadersStatus`** (line 38):\n- `Continue` \u2014 continue to the next filter\n- `StopIteration` \u2014 stop iterating; must call `continueDecoding()`/`continueEncoding()` to resume\n- `ContinueAndDontEndStream` \u2014 continue iteration but delay end_stream, allowing the filter to inject a body later\n- `StopAllIterationAndBuffer` \u2014 stop all iteration (headers, data, trailers); buffer incoming data; 413 on overflow\n- `StopAllIterationAndWatermark` \u2014 stop all iteration; use watermarks for flow control\n\n**`FilterDataStatus`** (line 129):\n- `Continue` \u2014 continue; buffered data is flushed\n- `StopIterationAndBuffer` \u2014 stop; buffer data\n- `StopIterationAndWatermark` \u2014 stop; use watermarks for backpressure\n- `StopIterationNoBuffer` \u2014 stop; discard buffered data\n\n**`FilterTrailersStatus`** (line 171):\n- `Continue` \u2014 continue\n- `StopIteration` \u2014 stop; must call `continueDecoding()`/`continueEncoding()` to resume\n\nThe filter's `IterationState` enum (`filter_manager.h:211-218`) tracks the current state: `Continue`, `StopSingleIteration`, `StopAllBuffer`, or `StopAllWatermark`.\n\n---\n\n## Q3: Router and Upstream\n\n### How the router obtains the target cluster and selects a host\n\nThe router filter (`source/common/router/router.h:298`, class `Filter`) is the terminal HTTP decoder filter. Its `decodeHeaders()` method (`source/common/router/router.cc:440`) performs:\n\n1. **Route lookup** (line 471): `route_ = callbacks_->route()` \u2014 obtains the route from the cached route in the `ActiveStream`.\n\n2. **Cluster lookup** (lines 523-534): Gets the thread-local cluster from the cluster manager:\n   ```cpp\n   Upstream::ThreadLocalCluster* cluster =\n       config_->cm_.getThreadLocalCluster(route_entry_->clusterName());\n   ```\n   Returns 503 if the cluster is unknown.\n\n3. **Host selection** (line 700): Calls `cluster->chooseHost(this)` where `this` is the `LoadBalancerContext`. The router implements `Upstream::LoadBalancerContextBase` (line 300), providing methods like `computeHashKey()`, `metadataMatchCriteria()`, `determinePriorityLoad()`, and `hostSelectionRetryCount()` that inform the load balancer's decision.\n\n4. **Connection pool acquisition** (line 756 in `continueDecodeHeaders()`): `createConnPool(*cluster, selected_host)` creates a `GenericConnPool` to obtain an upstream connection.\n\n### The role of UpstreamRequest and the upstream filter chain\n\n`UpstreamRequest` (`source/common/router/upstream_request.h:67`) is created at `router.cc:842`:\n```cpp\nUpstreamRequestPtr upstream_request = std::make_unique<UpstreamRequest>(\n    *this, std::move(generic_conn_pool), can_send_early_data, can_use_http3,\n    allow_multiplexed_upstream_half_close_);\n```\n\nAs documented in the header file comments (lines 42-66), `UpstreamRequest` manages the full lifecycle of forwarding a request to an upstream host:\n\n**Request path**: Data arrives via `acceptHeadersFromRouter()` (line 81), `acceptDataFromRouter()` (line 82), `acceptTrailersFromRouter()` (line 83), and `acceptMetadataFromRouter()` (line 84). These pass data to the `UpstreamFilterManager`, which iterates through upstream HTTP filters until reaching the terminal `UpstreamCodecFilter`. The `UpstreamCodecFilter` sends data to the upstream connection; if the connection isn't ready yet, it returns `StopAllIteration` and the `FilterManager` buffers data.\n\n**Connection establishment**: `UpstreamRequest` implements `GenericConnectionPoolCallbacks`. When the connection pool has a connection ready, `onPoolReady()` (line 120) is called, providing a `GenericUpstream` which wraps the upstream codec stream. When the pool fails, `onPoolFailure()` (line 117) triggers error handling.\n\n**Response path**: Upstream responses arrive via the `UpstreamCodecFilter`'s codec bridge, traverse the upstream filter chain in reverse, and reach `UpstreamRequestFilterManagerCallbacks`'s encode functions. These call through `UpstreamRequest`'s `decodeHeaders()`/`decodeData()`/`decodeTrailers()` methods (lines 96-98), which in turn call the router's `RouterFilterInterface::onUpstream[X]()` methods.\n\n### How the response flows back to the downstream\n\nThe router filter's `onUpstreamHeaders()` (`source/common/router/router.cc:1702`) processes the upstream response:\n\n1.         Code Changes (1)
        
1. WRITE /logs/agent/investigation.md
# Envoy HTTP Filter Chain Architecture

## Q1: Listener to Connection Manager

### How the listener accepts a TCP connection and hands it off

When a downstream client opens a TCP connection to Envoy, the OS-level accept is handled by `ActiveTcpListener::onAccept()` (`source/common/listener_manager/active_tcp_listener.cc:80`). This method performs connection limit checks, then calls `onAcceptWorker()` (line 109), which optionally rebalances the connection across worker threads via `ConnectionBalancer::pickTargetHandler()` (line 120-125). If the connection stays on the current worker, it creates an `ActiveTcpSocket` and calls `onSocketAccepted()`.

The `ActiveTcpSocket` (`source/common/listener_manager/active_tcp_socket.h:28`) acts as a `ListenerFilterManager` and runs listener filters (e.g., TLS inspector, proxy protocol) before the connection proceeds. Once listener filters complete, `ActiveTcpSocket::newConnection()` is called, which delegates to `ActiveStreamListenerBase::newConnection()`.

### Network filter chain selection

The mechanism that selects which network filter chain to use is `FilterChainManagerImpl::findFilterChain()` (`source/common/listener_manager/filter_chain_manager_impl.h:193`). This is called at `source/common/listener_manager/active_stream_listener_base.cc:30`:

```cpp
const auto filter_chain = config_->filterChainManager().findFilterChain(*socket, *stream_info);
```

`FilterChainManagerImpl` uses a multi-level matching hierarchy to select the appropriate filter chain based on connection properties:
1. **Destination port** (`DestinationPortsMap`)
2. **Destination IP** (`DestinationIPsTrie`)
3. **Server name** (SNI) (`ServerNamesMap`)
4. **Transport protocol** (`TransportProtocolsMap`)
5. **Application protocol** (ALPN) (`ApplicationProtocolsMap`
... (truncated)
